  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_820944fa-599e-4008-9f84-5395083de68c'

<div id="review_1122972381" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1122972381" />
    <a title="Mario" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16628840-mario"><img alt="Mario" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588674821p2/16628840.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1122972381?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario" href="/user/show/16628840-mario">Mario</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788610000955" href="/book/show/17879745-devojka-od-papira">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1122972381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6283005462075093242">First of all, I really love Guillaume Musso, some of his books are on my top favorite list. And I really enjoyed this book, up until last 40 pages, where all went downhill for me.<br/>The 'big twist' at the end, left me feeling so betrayed as a reader, and I felt like it was so unnecessary. It made me hate some of the characters. I would love the book if it didn't happen. And some parts were so frustrating to read. Few times I wanted to throw this book out of the window and have a car ran over it.<br/>I w</span>
  <span id="freeText6283005462075093242" style="display:none">First of all, I really love Guillaume Musso, some of his books are on my top favorite list. And I really enjoyed this book, up until last 40 pages, where all went downhill for me.<br />The 'big twist' at the end, left me feeling so betrayed as a reader, and I felt like it was so unnecessary. It made me hate some of the characters. I would love the book if it didn't happen. And some parts were so frustrating to read. Few times I wanted to throw this book out of the window and have a car ran over it.<br />I will continue reading his books, and I hope his other books won't leave me feeling like this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6283005462075093242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

No exceptions.<br>This book was on the most visible shelves in almost every bookstore. Please!!!<br>As if it ever counted for me to read what everyone else reads. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514477227ra/24780903.gif" width="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But, yeah, I did. The kind of bored when you want to close the book and rate it as a one star. I don't have a lot of one-stared books. The author must have a real talent, potential and must try really hard to annoy me to that extent. <br>This Musso! He did. I was skipping the pages by reading only two-three words. Overwritten sentences, oversubscribed scenes, undeveloped characters, unreasonable actions, unnecessary and irritable descriptions of rich Hollywood life, cliché used after cliché.<br>What saved this book? The ending! It wasn't the most beautiful and influencing one, no, nothing particular. But it really did save this book making me raise my rating from one star to two. And I was always rater-for-the-last-chapter-person, so... Good job. If only the middle of the book was as good as the ending. <div id="review_609848527" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/609848527" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5301718-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483927829p2/5301718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/609848527?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/5301718-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer609848527" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1312013152691434877">Anyone who has ever talked to me knows that I have a tendency of over analyzing things,(and now all of you who come across this review will know that too), it doesn't matter what, it can be everyday moments, words, songs, gestures, books, really, if it can be thought of I can over analyze it. <br/>Sometimes that is a bad thing, I often miss interpret people or think things are way more deep than they are, also , because of this, I have the incredible ability of making the easiest things as confusing </span>
  <span id="freeText1312013152691434877" style="display:none">Anyone who has ever talked to me knows that I have a tendency of over analyzing things,(and now all of you who come across this review will know that too), it doesn't matter what, it can be everyday moments, words, songs, gestures, books, really, if it can be thought of I can over analyze it. <br />Sometimes that is a bad thing, I often miss interpret people or think things are way more deep than they are, also , because of this, I have the incredible ability of making the easiest things as confusing as possible. But, there are times when this tendency of imagining too much just magically works out and makes a certain experience just a whole lot better and i can say that it happened with this book.<br />When I decided to read it I must admit I had no expectations. Great premise, but lately there has been many authors who manage to ruin books that otherwise could have been perfectly good, I just figured that with " girl on paper" the same would happen and surprisingly it didn't. I actually enjoyed the book very much but it was a 3 stars for me until the final chapters and I have to say that the fourth star may be the product of me over thinking, again.<br />The thing is (and PLEASE feel free to comment and give me your opinion) I don't think that Tom and his "Billie" had that happy ending that the book described, almost in the end you find out that what you have been reading is the process of creation of the book you have in your hands, why and when it was created. You have the book he is talking about and writing with you ALL the time. Which makes me conclude that obviously everything that you are reading happened before he finished writing it, before he published it.<br />If that is true, then how did "billie" find him in one of his book tours? How is he telling us about this encounter if it happens after the book has been published?<br />And here is where the book became really precious to me, he didn't meet her after he found out the truth, what he wrote, what he shows us, what he makes us believe in didn't happen, he wants it to happen, that is the future he imagines for them, but it is not real, at least, not yet and the truth is, we'll never know. We want to believe in him and he wants to believe in it too, but we don't know if that is going to happen. He writes that ending hoping that "Billie" will pick up his book and discover their story seen through his eyes and maybe, just maybe, she'll do exactly what the book told us she would. But we'll never know because before their story was truly over the book was out.<br />I wish there was a way for me to talk to the author, to ask him about my theory, to find out if he thought of that when writing his novel, but again, I won't get the answers I wanted and perhaps it is for the best, maybe I'm just over analyzing again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1312013152691434877" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_306384444" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Lynn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3684725-lynn"><img alt="Lynn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573035847p2/3684725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/306384444?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynn" href="/user/show/3684725-lynn">Lynn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781908313058" href="/book/show/12437071-the-girl-on-paper">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3684725-lynn?shelf=fiction-womens">fiction-womens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer306384444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8504606184810790709">The Girl on Paper is the antithesis of fiction. I picked this book up purely because of the striking cover and the drop line that "She fell out of a book....." Previously never being drawn to Musso's work I was intrigued by the premise of this story, which reminded me of Cornelia Funke's brilliant Inkheart series and wondered how it could be transferred into the adult market.<br/><br/>Starting with such a depressive note made it easier for the characters to evolve by the introspection of their lives toget</span>
  <span id="freeText8504606184810790709" style="display:none">The Girl on Paper is the antithesis of fiction. I picked this book up purely because of the striking cover and the drop line that "She fell out of a book....." Previously never being drawn to Musso's work I was intrigued by the premise of this story, which reminded me of Cornelia Funke's brilliant Inkheart series and wondered how it could be transferred into the adult market.<br /><br />Starting with such a depressive note made it easier for the characters to evolve by the introspection of their lives together. As the main character, Author Tom Boyd, grows from a very two dimensional personality into a fully rounded, likeable guy we are introduced to his life through the depictions of the highs and lows of his life so far. When Billie arrives into his story, the rich tapestry that has been unravelling for some time starts to knit back together. <br /><br />I loved being on this journey with Tom, Milo and Carole. Totally believable people in a wildly unbelievable situation. This book was a pleasure to read and pure escapism!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8504606184810790709" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer14413976997138883925">Ack, I didn’t care for this book. Every time a character is introduced, there’s a paragraph describing their appearance, personality, and how they feel about each of the other characters. Show, don’t tell!<br/><br/>I found the narrator genuinely unlikeable. Later in the novel he’s more tolerable, but when he spends the first 100 pages moping, that doesn’t start us on good terms. Nor did I care for the celebrity world of privilege in which he operates. <br/><br/>Not to mention how unrealistic the whole thing is. Not</span>
  <span id="freeText14413976997138883925" style="display:none">Ack, I didn’t care for this book. Every time a character is introduced, there’s a paragraph describing their appearance, personality, and how they feel about each of the other characters. Show, don’t tell!<br /><br />I found the narrator genuinely unlikeable. Later in the novel he’s more tolerable, but when he spends the first 100 pages moping, that doesn’t start us on good terms. Nor did I care for the celebrity world of privilege in which he operates. <br /><br />Not to mention how unrealistic the whole thing is. Not the woman appearing out of the pages of a book, but the narrator’s life in the supposedly real world. I can’t think of a single author, except perhaps JK, who is afforded star status equal to that of A-list actors. The whole story is littered with preposterous events. Not to mention the ending. <br /><br />Things picked up towards the second half of the book, but not enough for me to feel like the book was enjoyable. <br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1784634500" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8850507067974026101">Okay, so... My best friend pretty much shoved this book in my direction and told me I had to read it. And as a good friend, I trusted her words and decided to give it a chance. I slightly regret it now. <br/>Do not confuse my regret for not liking the book. Because I did. My regret is completely connected to the fact that the book gave me so much anxiety and I was almost on life support by the end.<br/>At the beggining I wasn't that commited to this story, but as the pages went on, I found myself stuck in</span>
  <span id="freeText8850507067974026101" style="display:none">Okay, so... My best friend pretty much shoved this book in my direction and told me I had to read it. And as a good friend, I trusted her words and decided to give it a chance. I slightly regret it now. <br />Do not confuse my regret for not liking the book. Because I did. My regret is completely connected to the fact that the book gave me so much anxiety and I was almost on life support by the end.<br />At the beggining I wasn't that commited to this story, but as the pages went on, I found myself stuck in this world where a book character magically came to life. As a writer myself, I couldn't help but imagine what would happen, how I would react if one of my characters appered to me one odd day. <br />By the end I was so entraced with the book, I was so inside of the story that I could feel all of the emotions with the characters. <br />My regret is due to the fact that I doubted the book when I first started it. My regret is due to the fact that I hadn't read this book before. My regret is due to the fact that I don't regret reading at all.<br />Thank you Camila. And thank you Guillaume.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1148158474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1148158474" />
    <a title="Coraline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38574254-coraline"><img alt="Coraline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455107342p2/38574254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1148158474?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Coraline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Coraline" href="/user/show/38574254-coraline">Coraline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789737243102" href="/book/show/13626760-fata-de-h-rtie">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38574254-coraline?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38574254-coraline?shelf=want-to-reread">want-to-reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1148158474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5271694153489666696">I've been wanting to read this book for a long time, but for some reason I kept postponing it. <b>
  <i>The Paper Girl</i>
</b> is... I don't know, I have no words to describe it.<br/><br/>Although it passes as a romance book, I would rather categorize it as an adventure and humor book. In any case, it's not cheesy at all or anything like that. It's an absolutely gorgeous book, extremely cleverly written and incredibly surprising. You have to read it to understand exactly what I mean.<br/><br/>There was no moment when you could </span>
  <span id="freeText5271694153489666696" style="display:none">I've been wanting to read this book for a long time, but for some reason I kept postponing it. <b>
  <i>The Paper Girl</i>
</b> is... I don't know, I have no words to describe it.<br /><br />Although it passes as a romance book, I would rather categorize it as an adventure and humor book. In any case, it's not cheesy at all or anything like that. It's an absolutely gorgeous book, extremely cleverly written and incredibly surprising. You have to read it to understand exactly what I mean.<br /><br />There was no moment when you could guess what is coming next or how it will end. Although it has an impressive collection of plot twists, they are not the kind of forced plot twists that you encounter in series and that you get tired of at some point.<br /><br />There were also countless moments when I could identify with the characters and countless times when I fumbled for the phone to photograph various passages from the book. Guillaume Musso has an indisputable talent for writing fiction in a way that makes you confuse it with reality.<br /><br />Tl;dr: This book is brilliant and worth reading at least once.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5271694153489666696" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2228239377" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2228239377" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30833806-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583342625p2/30833806.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2228239377?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/30833806-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781906040888" href="/book/show/15958671-the-girl-on-paper">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2228239377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16803986020888233500"> I was first introduced to this author by someone I seen in a long time but the author stuck with me. His way of writing characters shine off the page and for me at least means I all ways end up feeling a deep connection to them. This time the author chose to set his book on the themes of a writer who is struggling to live up to his own hype and also the trouble he is facing in his personal life. <br/><br/><br/> Once again the author managed to captivate me from the first few chapters. We are first introduced </span>
  <span id="freeText16803986020888233500" style="display:none"> I was first introduced to this author by someone I seen in a long time but the author stuck with me. His way of writing characters shine off the page and for me at least means I all ways end up feeling a deep connection to them. This time the author chose to set his book on the themes of a writer who is struggling to live up to his own hype and also the trouble he is facing in his personal life. <br /><br /><br /> Once again the author managed to captivate me from the first few chapters. We are first introduced to our hero Tom Boyd. This is someone who on the surface could come across very superficial. The supers star author who completely falls apart under the pressure of fame. But the author has selected a story for him that will make you fight for his side. This is a story of a kid who came from nothing and has fought tooth and nail for everything he has got. In the process, he has taken other with him in the hopes of giving them a better life. With these people, we also get a supporting cast that has flesh to them. I was given enough from them so as not to make them feel like cardboard people. As for Billie Our fictional heroine from a book within a book. She is detailed and gives breath back into our writer's life. At times feeling over the top with her blasé attitude she fits well and throughout the book, we get to feel a connection with a person that within the context of the book is not flesh and blood entirely. <br /><br /><br /> This is a story that is told to us in an easy manner. What is essentially a romance book takes on some very dark topics and leads our band of charters to some place some may find hard to read. I felt it added a balance to the book that otherwise I probably would have lost interest in after the first few chapters. It all told makes it hard not to connect with these people on an emotional level. For our three friends, they carry a bond that has held them together since childhood. And while our author chose to test this to the limit at times I was all ways left feeling there would be hope for them. And when Billie falls into Tom's life it allows not only for all hell to break loose but also allows us to question what it truly means to be human. The only troubling part of this story for me at least was Tom's obsession with his ex-girlfriend. For me, it felt a little bit dark and sick with the way he chases after even after she has told him to leave her alone. But I guess this is the catalyst for everything to come.<br /><br /><br /> As I've said overall this is an enjoyable read, fast paced with enough emotion behind his characters to draw you into the plot. The fantasy elements Worked for me and give the story a lighter feeling than might otherwise have occurred and offset the darker tones. From Child abuse, addiction and life-threatening illness, this book does seem to cover the gambit. But for me, it was worth the time I put into it. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16803986020888233500" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_382020176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/382020176" />
    <a title="Shaz Goodwin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4422203-shaz-goodwin"><img alt="Shaz Goodwin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605022219p2/4422203.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/382020176?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shaz Goodwin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shaz Goodwin" href="/user/show/4422203-shaz-goodwin">Shaz Goodwin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781908313058" href="/book/show/12437071-the-girl-on-paper">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer382020176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12555231471293360224">Through a series of newspaper/magazine articles and emails the reader gains an insight into Tom’s success, Aurore’s success and the rise and fall of their relationship. I thought this was a unique way to give the reader background!<br/><br/>The story opens with Tom’s best friend and ‘business’ partner Milo trying to get into Tom’s luxury home in Malibu Colony. Breaking in he finds Tom unconscious and surrounded by pill boxes. Milo manages to get him out of his home. We find out that the special edition of</span>
  <span id="freeText12555231471293360224" style="display:none">Through a series of newspaper/magazine articles and emails the reader gains an insight into Tom’s success, Aurore’s success and the rise and fall of their relationship. I thought this was a unique way to give the reader background!<br /><br />The story opens with Tom’s best friend and ‘business’ partner Milo trying to get into Tom’s luxury home in Malibu Colony. Breaking in he finds Tom unconscious and surrounded by pill boxes. Milo manages to get him out of his home. We find out that the special edition of Tom’s last book has a major problem – only half of the book has been printed resulting in the publishers having to pulp 10,000 copies (minus the copy that Milo has). We also find out that an investment Milo made has gone wrong … leaving them bankrupt.<br /><br />We’re then introduced to Carole. All three of them grew up at MacArthur Park (a hangout for heroin addicts, criminal gangs and poverty). Their friendship is a theme that is explored in the story. Their childhood background is always just a whisper away from the lives they are living now.<br /><br />Back in Malibu, Tom throws the half-printed book in the trash. He swallows a handful of sleeping pills and tranquillisers. Having been woken from his drugged sleep by a storm, he finds a naked woman in his home. Enter Billie Donelly, a secondary character from his trilogy. She has fallen out of the half-printed book and convinces Tom that she really is Billie.<br /><br />Milo and Carole arrange sleep therapy for Tom but when he arrives, he realises they are going to have him committed. Escaping dramatically with Billie, the adventure begins …<br /><br />On their journey to Aurore in Mexico there is excitement and suspense. Starting out in Milo’s Bugatti, mishaps mean their transport downsizes (as does their luggage) eventually arriving on foot. There is also suspense and excitement with Milo and Carole locating and trying to catch up with the journey that Tom’s trashed copy of the half-finished book takes. The only remaining copy, it is central to Billie’s well-being. I’ve journeyed to America, Mexico, Rome, Paris and Asia and actually felt as if I’ve spent time there!<br /><br />There is also plenty of romance. The emotion builds between Tom and Billie and I felt quite distraught when it was time for Billie to go back to being a character between the pages of a book. We find out early on in the story that Milo has always loved Carole and become involved in them each having to come to terms with their own shadows. There is one dramatic scene, which shocked Milo but ultimately forced the truth to be told.<br /><br />Another unique factor for me is the two different narratives throughout The Girl on Paper. When we are with Tom, it’s a first person narrative and with Milo and Carole, third person. I thought this worked really well.<br /><br />As with ‘Where Would I be Without You?’ there are apt quotations at the beginning of each chapter that are relevant to what you are about to read. Loved this.<br /><br />The pace of the plot is fast with crises and resolution throughout. I loved the use of personification, for example on page 257:<br /><br />“The air was mild and the pale full moon was admiring its own reflection on the surface of the water.”<br /><br />The twist in the plot … amazing! I had absolutely no idea. Brilliant! I learnt something about myself after reflecting on my reaction…<br /><br />I’ll be looking out for The Angel’s Call which is due summer 2013.<br /><br />The Girl on Paper is translated by Emily Boyce and Anna Aitken.<br /><br />I would like to thank Gallic Books for a copy in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12555231471293360224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_251263343" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/251263343" />
    <a title="Rosie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3766837-rosie"><img alt="Rosie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595621534p2/3766837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/251263343?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rosie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rosie" href="/user/show/3766837-rosie">Rosie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781908313058" href="/book/show/12437071-the-girl-on-paper">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3766837-rosie?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer251263343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9286729818231462750">The idea of this book intrigued me straight away. The idea of a depressed, confused, writer on the road to self destruction over “his one true love”, saved by a character in his own novel. Now, for some this could seem quite far-fetched however it was pulled off fairly well. Hearing a summary of this book you know things aren’t going to be straight forward and you’re right. <br/><br/>Like I said, the plot was a great idea and an interesting one. However, towards the end I felt that it was going off the po</span>
  <span id="freeText9286729818231462750" style="display:none">The idea of this book intrigued me straight away. The idea of a depressed, confused, writer on the road to self destruction over “his one true love”, saved by a character in his own novel. Now, for some this could seem quite far-fetched however it was pulled off fairly well. Hearing a summary of this book you know things aren’t going to be straight forward and you’re right. <br /><br />Like I said, the plot was a great idea and an interesting one. However, towards the end I felt that it was going off the point and it was becoming far too… Out there, even for a fiction novel. I could swallow the fact a fictional girl has fallen out of his novels due to a misprint however I just couldn’t understand how a single book could travel from several different people’s possession… Also why it was even necessary to be told some of their backstories. Speaking of backstories, the ones of the four main characters (Tom, Milo, Carole and Billie) were very interesting and drove the story forward and gave them all great depth. Tom was a fantastic character, I’m always interested in the tortured writer type and he certainly had a dark past behind him! Billie was an interesting character to add to the mix and she definitely brought a life and energy to the story.<br /><br />The story started off brilliantly and I loved the prologue - telling us the details of Tom’s rise to fame and fall into depression through emails from fans and headlines in magazines/newspapers. As I mentioned before after a while the book started to drift from one thing to another, it was meant to be suspenseful and fast paced however I felt that it had the opposite effect on me and felt it was quite tedious/tiresome. However I kept reading and I’m pleased I did as there was a fantastic twist at the end that made it all worthwhile and really blew me away (despite having a feeling earlier on in the novel that this was where it’d end up). <br /><br />This book is great if you want to read something a bit out of the ordinary and to kill a bit of time. Stick with the book no matter how annoyed you get with it or impatient as it does pay off. I liked the way the novel ended as it seemed to sum everything up. There were some faults with the novel, I didn’t like how the copy of the book just seemed to end up everywhere and how people seemed to go to places with ease with hardly any money and dodgy passports… I also feel that more could be done with a plot like this. It’s such a good idea that it’s a shame it’s full potential didn’t come out in this novel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9286729818231462750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1699757011" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1699757011" />
    <a title="Aya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32740224-aya"><img alt="Aya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475251203p2/32740224.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1699757011?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aya" href="/user/show/32740224-aya">Aya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1699757011" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8930963951491292637">I got offered this book by one of my dearest friends. I've been wanting to read it for so long, mostly because I remember having devoured the previous one (Seras-tu là?) so avidly. And, once again, I was far from disappointed. The plot is worked out so amazingly that you find yourself driven by the constant need to run through the pages in order to connect the dots and get the fuller picture. It's an absolute page-turner. <br/>This book covered pretty much all the issues and frames of mind authors go</span>
  <span id="freeText8930963951491292637" style="display:none">I got offered this book by one of my dearest friends. I've been wanting to read it for so long, mostly because I remember having devoured the previous one (Seras-tu là?) so avidly. And, once again, I was far from disappointed. The plot is worked out so amazingly that you find yourself driven by the constant need to run through the pages in order to connect the dots and get the fuller picture. It's an absolute page-turner. <br />This book covered pretty much all the issues and frames of mind authors go through while plotting their stories, which was interesting to know, as it gave us a glimpse into the other side of this whole experience, emphasizing the fact that the author is to deliver a story which the reader will vivify through his imagination. This, of course, gives the author the creator privilege to deliberately plan the characters' lives and destinies. But does he perforce use that power to attain "justice"? </span>
  <a data-text-id="8930963951491292637" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RnFjcKKCEc1dEXPKEIbC822B/Ub0773pctDAEgNeIsjDeaPjJsARIexUxkwW/dTS4RaijHsdLG4agl+isSpEew==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }

Keira leaves her necklace behind in Adrian\'s apartment, sparking his interest as a scientist and fuelling his hopes for a rekindling of old passions. They follow maps written in the stars and clues buried within the earth, always guided by the slowly unraveling secrets of the strange object from Ethiopia. وعطائها الذي لا حدود له للمحبوب: &quot;كنت على استعداد لأن أصغر فتكبر..لأن أفشل لتنجح، لأن أخبو لتلمع..&quot;، ونوعية حبها الذي لا يقدره بل يتجاهله أو يقوم باستغلاله لصالح أهداف أقل أهمية منه بكثير، وأقل قيمة. &quot;ما زلت لا أدرك، لا أدرك كيف يتلاعب رجل بامرأة تحبه من دون أن يخاف للحظة مما يفعله نحوها!&quot;\n\nفي كل مرة و&quot;بعد كل خيبة أمل.. بعد كل محنة وكل نزوة.. كنت أحاول لملمة أجزائي لنفتح مجدداً صفحة بيضاء أخرى..&quot;، لكن &quot;البدايات الجديدة ما هي إلا كذبة&quot;.\n\nتستعيد الكاتبة ذكرياتها معه منذ البداية في مقهى خارج الوطن الذي غادرته للدراسة: &quot;الوطن الذي لو لم أغادره لما حدث كل هذا.. أتكون أنت عقابي على مغادرة وطن أحبني!..&quot;، وفكرة العقاب والثواب التي يسخر منها عزيز، تؤمن هي بها: &quot;مؤمنة أنا بيوم الحساب أكثر من أي شيء،&quot; لأنها تأمل عبرها أن ينال عزيز عقابه على ما اقترفه بحقها.\n\nقالت لهما العجوز الهندية غريبة الأطوار، دون سابق معرفة: &quot;هي متعبة منك..منك فقط..وأنت متعب من كل شيء..&quot;، وقالت لها &quot;هيفاء&quot; صديقتها الكويتية التي تتخاصم دائما وعزيز، بأنه لا يستحقها، وتقول جمانة له اليوم &quot;حبي لك كان أعمى يا عزيز..وأن هيفاء رأت فيك ما لم أره..&quot;، رأت الكذب المتسلسل والخيانة والإنكار الذي يشكك الآخر بنفسه وبعقله وإحساسه، وهي صفات تتجاهلها المرأة التي تحب رجلاً يحبها لكنه غير قادر على الالتزام بها. قال لها بصراحة: &quot;اسمعي.. أنا رجل لعوب.. أشرب وأعربد وأعاشر النساء.. لكنني أعود إليك في كل مرة..&quot;، وكانت تتحمل الأذى: &quot;تؤذينني عمداً وكأنك تفرغ في نفسي أحقادك وأوجاعك وأمراضك، تؤذيني عمداً باسم الحبّ..&quot;. وهي بالرغم من كل الحقائق والوقائع تعترف: &quot;لم أبكِ بحرقة إلا بسببك ولم أضحك من أعماقي إلا معك.. أليست بمعادلة صعبة..؟ يحلل لها زياد صديقهما المشترك الوضع: &quot;أحببته لدرجة أخافته!.. لم يكن قادراً على ضمك لقائمة نسائه ولم يتمكن من الابتعاد عنك.. أحبك لدرجة أنه كان يخشى عليك من نفسه.. كما كان يخشى منك في الوقت ذاته..&quot;\n\nكيف يلتقيان، وهو يؤمن بأن الغاية تبرر الوسيلة، وهي تؤمن &quot;بأن الوسيلة أحياناً أهم من الغاية!&quot;؟\n\n&quot;قلت لي يوماً بأن حكايات الحبّ الشرقية غالباً ما تنتهي بمأساة. واليوم أعرف بأنك كنت محقاً في هذا..&quot;\n\nتنقل الرواية بصدق عميق ما يدور في أعماق المرأة في حالة حب،ّ من أحاسيس وأفكار وتناقضات، إذ تظن أن الخيار الصعب إلى أقسى مداه يكمن في الحفاظ على مشاعر الحبّ الجياشة واستمرارها، على حساب التنكّر للذات الواعية والمدركة لتلاعب الطرف الآخر بها، لكنها بأي حال، وحتى في حال دفع الحساب، لن تحصل على مبتغاها.<\/span>\n  <a <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9019430669321838479">One of the most popular authors in France today. From his early childhood with reading books and plays, Guillaume Musso became convinced that one day, he too would write novels. After finishing high school in France, Guillaume Musso left for the United States at the age of 19. He spent several months in New York City, living with other young foreigners and earning his money by selling ice-cream. H</span>
  <span id="freeText9019430669321838479" style="display:none">One of the most popular authors in France today. From his early childhood with reading books and plays, Guillaume Musso became convinced that one day, he too would write novels. After finishing high school in France, Guillaume Musso left for the United States at the age of 19. He spent several months in New York City, living with other young foreigners and earning his money by selling ice-cream. He came home to France with his head filled with ideas for novels. The readers can easily see the influence his time in the United States has had on him, as the action in his books takes place overseas. He currently teaches in a high school in the south of France, all the while working on his novels. His first published novel was with Editions Anne Carriere in 2001: <i>Skidamarink</i>, this novel did not reach out to the masses however, but his following novels published on XO Editions have all been hugely successful, some of them translated into 20 languages. His novel, <i>Afterwards</i>, has been adapted to the big screen and was in cinemas January 2009, starring John Malkovich, Evangeline Lily and Romain Duris.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9019430669321838479" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/10740837-la-fille-de-papier">Quotes from La fille de papier</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;إن الروابط تُعقَد وتنفرط، هذه هي الحياة. ذات صباح، يظل واحد ويرحل الثاني من دون أن نعرف أبداً لماذا. لا أستطيع منح كل شيءٍ للآخر، وسيف داموقليس ذاك معلق فوق رقبتي. لا أريد بناء حياتي على المشاعر، لأن المشاعر تتبدل. إنها هشة وغير أكيدة. إنك تعتقد أنها عميقة، بينما هي خاضعة لتنورة عابرة أو ابتسامة مصطنعة. إني أمارس الموسيقى لأن الموسيقى لن تفارق حياتي. إني أحب الكتب، لأن الكتب ستظل دوماً هنا. ثم... إني لا أعرف أناساً يحبون بعضهم مدى الحياة.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/1184448">55 likes</a>
            </nobr>

          </div>
